RATING: 4
[i]tl;dr - Don't assume too much strategy, but appreciate the light decision space and tetris-like stacking that Patchwork gives you. When you can whip through three games in about fifteen minutes, you know you've found a good two-player filler.[/i]
[COLOR=#CCCCFF]____________________________[/COLOR]

Patchwork is a little abstract that has rightly gotten a lot of buzz. Approached as a light, fun, game, I can't think of many flaws -- I really enjoy playing this one with my wife and we love the flow of building your quilt, acquiring buttons, and tetris-ing everything together. 

However, I can see how many gamers wouldn't like this one. There's a lot of randomness in how the pieces are shuffled out and sometimes you are forced to pass just because of bad tile distribution, giving your opponent a huge advantage. All things considered, I'll probably end up playing this one more casually than competitively, but be aware that it can be unbalanced (as any two-player game) in competitive play. 

For me, this just doesn't flip my lid, which is a reversal of where I was at several plays ago. I would have said that the luck factor is fine, there's mitigation, that it's still pleasant to build your quilts -- nope, my wife and I are far too competitive for this one, and it won't be sticking in my collection.

RATING: 8
Absolutely brilliant. I did not expect this from Uwe who I almost considered a lost designer of late. Lost to making games too convoluted and heavy. 

Patchwork is a nice mix of planning a step or two ahead, blocking your opponent and seizing the opportunities. It offers trade-offs between getting the best tile for you and denying your opponent something. And again (like in Le Havre) your victory points are your resources.

Best of all, this plays in 20 minutes and still manages to be a satisfying experience.

RATING: 7
Patchwork is a nice two player game. It's quick to explain, easy to play and it has all the qualities of a well designed game... but it's also barely OK, at least in my opinion.

Don't get me wrong, playing Patchwork is actually fairly enjoyable, especially when you are in the mood to play something "relaxing", so to speak. It allows you to play an engine building game without a huge number crunching and the complexity typical of these kinds of games. Still it's also very repetitive and it gets old pretty quickly, therefore I really don't understand how this game got to number 38 on the general ranking on BGG. I don't usually care so much about these sort of things, but I really believe that this game is overrated by the community here.

While there's nothing really wrong with Patchwork as a design, there are much better 2-player games on the market right now. It's a good way to spend 20 minutes with your significant other, but not good enough to be so highly regarded. Just an alright game.

RATING: 8
A light game with plenty of strategic depth, and honestly it can have some pretty cutthroat opportunities if you wish to go that route.

A definite hit for us, as it offers a quick play time with a varying depth of strategy. This is the only game we own that we have played back to back, and on every occasion it has come out, it has been played back to back.

The payoff of buttons throughout the game is a little moment of joy as you see how well your board is coming along. Every game I've played so far feels like there is no way I can complete my quilt by the end of the game, but I always manage to get within a few spaces. What is also fun is that our scores improve every time we play. We're not sure what we're doing differently, but we're getting significantly better somehow!

Awesome game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.1
This is a cool little game.  It's so easy to learn and play.  Every time I play, I want to try a different strategy.  The only draw back is how overly-balanced the game is, which might be a plus for many people. There is no way at all to get to an early lead.  Even if you do something really smart and get the right piece for the right price at the right time, you will still be opening up your opponent to gain something as well.  In fact, it kind of feels like one player could do almost nothing and it would still be a close game,  The counterbalance to this is how you construct your quilt board.  The one thing that matters more than anything else is fitting the fabric pieces well on your board.  This also means that very often it will be the person who gets the 7 bonus points for making a 7x7 grid who wins, but not necessarily.  Making a 7x7 grid costs you the opportunity to use larger pieces at the end of the game which are needed to cover large areas on your board.  Anyway, the games are ALWAYS close.  It doesn't matter how much "better" or "worse" you play, the game is going to be close.  There are too many balances in the scoring for one person to just slaughter another.  Nevertheless, this is a very fun very replayable game that can be found for a reasonable price.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Patchwork is definitely a cute little 2-player game and would be easy to bring to any family member, even ones who don't game.

As a rule, I don't enjoy abstract strategy games, so I didn't buy this one for me. My partner had a significantly better time with it than I did. Make no mistake, past the cute exterior, this is still a typical abstract game of trying to make moves and countermoves. The board tile arranging is nice but unless you both A. Run out of space for new tiles and B. Lose because of that fact, it never comes into play during that actual game. It's just sort of a thing to entertain you while you check for the next tile you need.

There are a lot of different unilateral and mixed strategies to the game but the key difference is the starting tile placement. If you take tile placement too lightly, you can find yourself in a horrible position for the entire game. Once a player begins to dominate tile selection (due to starting position), it's ridiculously difficult to stop them without tanking your economy, which they might be able to recover from while you grab up buttons.

Due to the abstract nature and the critical component of player snowballing, I can't really rate this game too high. It's good to kill a half hour with my partner before moving on to something where the choices feel more meaningful.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
In Patchwork, two players compete to build the most aesthetic (and high-scoring) patchwork quilt on a personal 9x9 game board. To start play, lay out all of the patches at random in a circle and place a marker directly clockwise of the 2-1 patch. Each player takes five buttons — the currency/points in the game — and someone is chosen as the start player.

RATING: 5.5
This game feels a bit, to me, like Jaipur and Pandemic where the game has been so meticulously playtested and balanced, that you could basically slot in any two random people and get the same end results every time. They give the impression of making choices, but it all comes back to where the designer wants you by the end. There's no way to go massively over on your board, nor under. What you miss in squares is made up for in buttons, and whether you go heavy on buttons or on large tiles, you still end up with a similar score as your opponent.

I can imagine that, after a lot of plays, you could really start to play by looking ahead and really trying to kneecap your opponent at the market, but even there, I feel like the game is so balanced that it probably won't accomplish much in the end run.

I like that it has easy to learn rules, and I certainly wouldn't mind playing the game many dozens of times, but the overly-balanced nature of it makes it feel like my involvement is unnecessary, and so I may as well play something else.

RATING: 7
Everything from the size of the box to game length and the simplicity of the rules reminds of the Kosmos two-player line.  Patchwork is a game about balancing needs for puzzle pieces to make a quilt against income and time.  Information is completely open.  If that sounds brain-burny, it really isn't because choices are limited each turn. The net result is a charming and clever game.

The artwork - with each of those puzzle-pieces redolent of scraps of fabric and buttons the currency - significantly adds to the charm.  Production quality is good.

RATING: 8
Απλό και γρήγορο 2-player παιχνίδι από τον κ.Rosenberg. Κάθε γύρα αγοράζεις ένα tile και το τοποθετείς στο ταμπλό σου. Σκοπός είναι να γεμίσεις όσο πιο πολύ μπορείς το ταμπλό σου, ενώ ρόλο παίζει το turn order και το πότε θα ενεργοποιήσεις το εισόδημα σου. Το κάθε σχήμα στα tiles είναι μοναδικό.

Η αλληλεπίδραση όπως και στα περισσότερα eurogames περιορίζεται στο ποιος παίκτης θα προλάβει το τάδε tile, ενώ υπάρχουν και κάποια μικρά tiles δώρο σε όποιον τρέξει στο turn order, που μπαλώνουν τρύπες στο ταμπλό σου. Τίμιο παιχνίδι, συνιστάται σε όσους αρέσκονται στο tile placement.

Καλή πρώτη εντύπωση καθώς γενικά μου αρέσει το special element, δεν ξέρω πως πάει από replayability αλλά είναι ιδανικό για euro ζευγάρια και όχι μόνο.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
:arrowE: [u]Synopsis[/u]:
You're making a quilt by spending buttons to acquire patches of various sizes. Those patches have a cost in two currencies, however--not just buttons, but [i]time[/i]. Each patch requires that you move your marker some amount of distance up the time track to the impending end point, which triggers the close of the game. The player whose marker is last takes turns until they pass the other player's marker, etc... Some patches come with buttons, increasing your button income after passing certain intervals. But you can never earn time, only lose it. Points are scored for accumulated buttons, as well as the difference between covered and uncovered spots on your quilt.

:arrowE: [u]What I like most[/u]:
The grueling crunch. Carefully balancing the expenditure of time and buttons is very, very difficult. This is a two-player game. You either win or lose, and the other player is likely calculating the most efficient path to shredding your score. Trying to figure out the time versus buttons versus quilt coverage versus income equation is very crunchy, and the game is actually quite brutal in typical Uwe Rosenberg fashion. Quilting has never been so devastating.

:arrowE: [u]What I like least[/u]:
This is often described as a "wife game" (a moniker I find distasteful) because it has a low barrier to entry and has a "cute theme," meaning it's great for dumb women, right? Wrong. First, that's a ludicrous and sexist distinction. Second, as I noted above, this game is no innocent cakewalk, it's a serious and challenge competition. /soapbox

RATING: 9
For such a simple game, this game was a pleasant surprise; it combines a multitude of decisions under a very simple rule set. It is a lovely melody of engine-building, tile valuation, turn-order manipulation, and a Tetris like abstract puzzle that creates some interesting blocking decisions. For casual gamers, the rules are simple and the purchasing limitations provide a focus. But for competitive gamers, there is no in-game randomization and the game invites players to think several turns ahead. The end result is a game that may just be the ultimate filler... quick, easy to learn, and enjoyed by casual and competitive gamers alike.

RATING: N/A
05.01.02.02
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Brilliant, simple but quite deep two-player game, very different by any other design by Uwe.

Rules are straightforward. You can only do one of the two actions (last player on a timetrack moves):
1) buy a patch and sew it on your quilt, paying with buttons, and advance on a timetrack;
2) advance on the timetrack until you reach the opponent and gain buttons for the spaces moved.
If you pass one of a series of special spot, gain a mini-patch (if you pass over it first) or buttons.

The simple, clever combination of a timetrack mechanic (à la Thebes) and a tetris-like puzzle is very elegant and compelling, and the unusual theme is quite engaging.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Such an excellent design! The mechanics are clever and efficient, the playing time matches the depth, and the player interaction strikes just the right balance between indirect and direct. I can't quite put my finger on why but Uwe Rosenberg's games are always so... nice. Maybe it's because they are just as much about beating your own score as they are about beating your opponents.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
:d10-2:

Yep, this one has more depth than I had thought upon first glance. After the first two plays, I had a suspicion that there was more to be seen. And on plays three and four, I saw it.

The economics of the game works out that tile prices are basically balanced around six costs/benefits:

1) Button cost, i.e. VP cost
2) Time cost, i.e. finite resource equal between players
3) Tempo cost, i.e. actions given up to the other player in order to do this particular action
4) Button gain, i.e. regular source of VPs which rewards early investment
5) Spatial coverage, i.e. one time VP gains
6) Shape irregularity, i.e. loss of chance at bonus VPs and/or potential spatial coverage

All of these concerns interact with one another in interesting ways. BUT, the [i]one[/i] cost that can be entirely negated with good play is #6. Shape irregularity. If you plan to get the exactly fitting pieces and place them correctly, you can gain more of the other benefits while skirting the typical costs associated. This means that the more advanced you get, the more the geometry of the game takes center stage. Thus, a game that seems to be a cute, light economic engine game becomes a brain puzzling spatial organization test paired with a savagely clever turn order and tile opportunity dance.

I really want to play this well.

RATING: 8
Oh man, my wife loves Patchwork. She's a crafter, for a start, so the theme is right on the button (haha) for her but she also can't get enough of the Tetris-style puzzle that the game offers. Me, I find it extremely stressful knowing every square I fail to patch is going to cost me two points at the end of the game, and I feel like I'm in a mad scramble just to avoid absolute failure. It's worse even than Agricola's constant feed-your-family dread. I'm yet to beat her, and in fact I'm yet to score positive points in a game, but I'll definitely play this again.

RATING: 10
A two currency economic 2-player game with a spatial tetris-like dimension to it.  Although it plays in 15ish minutes, it creates a lot of thinkiness and opportunities for clever play.  The random initial set-up ensures multiple games will often play out differently; however, there is no danger of "white-to-play-and-win" as the leap-frogging aspect creates a deeper, more nuanced game.

Hard to believe it's a Uwe Rosenberg or that he managed to put so much depth into a game with two rules.  Great game!

RATING: 8.5
Patchwork is a fantastic 2 player game that becomes more enjoyable the more I play it. The simplicity of the setup and teaching time make it very accessible, but the depth of strategy with multiple plays make this a classic in my collection. I love Uwe Rosenberg's two player games (Agricola: All Creatures Big and Small is also a winner) and I am very excited to see if he will release more. The theme of this game is perfect. I never thought that I would say I have a blast playing a game about quilting but the more I play it the more I realize this is the best theme for this Tetris style puzzler. The price, the time to play, the ease of learning and the enjoyable theme make this game a very strong recommendation for me and one of my favorite two player only games of all time. The game is cute, but it's still enjoyable for guys to play and get into. This game feels like the Little Big Planet of the tabletop world. Very kid friendly and whimsical but deep enough that any age will have fun. Buy this for yourself, buy it for a friend, we need to support these two player releases because they are perfect for coffee shop date nights with a spouse or a lunch filler with a friend. Good job Uwe and Mayfair, bravo.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a fantastic two player game, with such a lot to think about and a surprising range of tactical problems arising from what seems like a simple set up. Which should be no surprise, given Uwe Rosenberg's track record, other than the 'simple set up' part.

Patchwork feels really fresh, with an offbeat theme and design elements we hadn't seen before - though the spatial puzzle & rotating choice of pieces has since been partially recycled in Cottage Garden, with elements in A Feast for Odin and elsewhere.

The heart of the game though is the delicate balancing act between the cost of pieces in both time and 'money' and their benefits in terms of income and both space covered and their fit with the Tetris-y puzzle you're solving. 

And, in case that's not enough, you really should be looking out for how the choices you make impact on your opponent in terms of the options your move gives them - what looks like a less than ideal move can force them into a tactical dead end, particularly if they're low on funds, and open new options for you. Superb.

RATING: 6
Going into this one, I thought it would be one of those light, fluffy games, where everything is balanced to where scores will just be close, and the decisions would all kind of come out in the wash.

However, this is not true at all, as you can definitely play well or poorly, and scores can be quite lopsided. It was nice to see that the decisions mattered a great deal! You'll be doing a lot of calculating on which tile scores the most points per unit of time spent to acquire it, while also trying to avoid setting up your opponent for good tiles.

The game still didn't really grab me though, and I can't put my finger on why that is. I think it just ended up a bit on the abstract side for my tastes, but is still a game I'd happily play along with if someone else wanted to play.

RATING: 7
Based on 1 play:

I can see why this is so beloved. This is a nice, accessible game that 1) seamlessly blends abstract spatial puzzling with light resource/economy management and 2) plays fast. I would happily, unreservedly recommend it to folks just getting into the hobby looking for a quick, replayable 2p game.

For someone with a robust 2p collection already though, I'm not sure how long this will stick with me. For now I look forward to playing again (although having won my first game and achieved a satisfying score, I'm not sure what I'd do differently). Seems like a good game to bring along any old place, and play with anyone who will sit and listen to the 1 minute rules explanation. It seems like a good "vacation" game - portable, easy to remember the rules, meaty but still playable after a bottle of wine or a few beers. Is it what I'll reach for when I'm home and want to really test my puzzling skills against my spouse, though? Over YINSH or Hive? Probably not.

RATING: 8
A neat economic game with low rules overhead to make it very accessible.

You are balancing the spending of two currencies with one (buttons) serving as a constraint, and the other (time) serving as a game clock.  Both currencies are spent in an effort to fill a game board.  Weighing the pros and cons of buttons vs. time costs lead to some interesting tipping points in the game.

What raises this game above normal filler games is how pieces are selected.  One can only choose a piece within three spaces of the last piece chosen.  This leads to some double-think and extortive piece selection to try to hem your opponent into less profitable moves.  Bolting this on top of the economic game discussed above makes it a great addition to my collection.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I was ignoring this game for a long time since the theme turned me really off. But now I am glad to give it a try (mainly because it was very cheap so I could include to my shipment).
This is a quick, tight and fun 2 player only game which reminds tetris a bit. There are three major things to consider when taking a tile - cost (number of buttons spent to buy it), time (how many time points you will move ahead on the time board when buying the tile) and the shape and size (how many fields can you cover with it and how will it fit into your board).
Some tiles have 1-3 buttons included on themselves and these serve as a source of income (there are several income thresholds in the game where you will gain buttons according to the buttons on your tiles), but these are more expensive (both in cost and time) that the tiles without buttons. 
You can choose only three of the tiles after the current position on the tile market. And you have infinite number of time points to spent, your button count is very tight (at least at the beginning of the game) so you should do your best to fill as much as possible (and maybe scoring 7x7 bonus)

What I like:
- this is very interesting economy game with three currencies (buttons, time and space) and you have to find out which is the most important for you to save at the moment. This leads to very interesting game decisions as you prefer different tiles according to the game stage and your progress.
- Games are quick, this can be finished under 15 minutes when both players are somewhat experienced with it.
- Visual aspect of the game is cute. I bet all women will like it (you mother, sister, girlfriend, wife..)
- you can see your progress in this game. First several games you will often have negative score, but as you learn it more and more, the score will rise - this is very satisfying 

What I dislike:
- I was not interested in this because of the theme. I thought game about needling? no thanks. But I was so wrong. The theme could be easily about building the city or something like that, it doesn't matter.
- the setup (randomization of the tiles) is a bit long and boring for me - I like to have all randomized a lot in my games, so I need to pay attention to this a lot before game. Problem is that the tiles are with different sizes so you must pick them carefully to provide true randomization.
- The game may feel a bit repetitive once you found how to play it properly. There is not much different strategies involved, you simply just try to do similar things in every game (but the tile offer is always different). But this is OK as I play this just as a relaxing 2 player game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
2 player game.  Spacial/abstract, which usually aren't my style game, but this one works.  You need to balance the acquisition of buttons, advancing in time too fast, filling the quilt spaces, double plays, and looking ahead on future pieces.

The first time we played, we concentrated way too much on neat and tidy quilts while ignoring pieces with buttons.  It resulted in massive negative scores.  After a few plays we found a better balance and started producing positive scores.

I ordered a bag of 100 random buttons from Amazon for $4.87 and will replace the cardboard buttons for real ones.

Update:

We've played it a few more times and have really come to like to nuances.  Tonight we played on teams (couple v couple) and it was a lot of fun.

RATING: 4
Seeing the notes I thought it was a joke. Second family game ? I have a hard time seeing this in this game. There's a huge random effect on the initial disposition. This effect gets even more present from the fact that a favorable disposition gets you more buttons, which gets you more points and coins to spend, and less for your adversary, all this considering you're tight on money for the first few turns. The only option the other player has to mitigate is catch up on the board on the other player and get money for it, sacrificing in the process precious board tiles that are also a currency, all of this while sacrificing a turn that the richest player will be able to potentially steal yet another button tiles.

In my opinion, strategy and mechanics are interesting, but a bit too much on the random side at set up =/

Overally I think many other games with better mechanics and theme are much more of that second spot (including the equally tetris-y Out of mine

RATING: N/A
Abstract: 2
Family: 2
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
THE perfect 2-player game. Moments to set up, taught in 5 min., can be grasped and enjoyed by kids in elementary school, but has depth that will challenge avid strategy gamers.

1) Initial state is random = Solid replayability
2) After setup, perfect information (nothing hidden or random) = Opportunity for deep strategic analysis
3) Limited options at any give time = Quick play (unless you're really working #2)
4) Warm, cuddly theme = Wide appeal to gamers of all sensitivity levels.
5) Quality components = Many years of enjoyment

Any game designer could take immense and well-deserved satisfaction to have created Patchwork. How incredible that this perfect gem shares a home shelf with the likes of Agricola, Fields of Arle, Caverna, Le Havre, and soon, A Feast For Odin!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

#: Best 2, 2
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Few small caveats this game takes up a little too much table space, it plays only with two (see cottage garden), and is essentially themeless. That said, this game is incredibly simple, satisfying and fun. It's like two player tetris with an economic element. I am convinced that going for the button cash is better than going for the perfect quilt (word looks wrong to me) as having more cash you can say yes to whatever and zip ahead to snag those useful single patches. I have seen people bemoan this games high rating. Yes it's not brass or powergrid, it doesn't feature plastic wizards or epic space battle. It's simpler than that, less grande. It's a fun two player puzzler to play after tea (dinner) with your significant other. You could gift this to almost anyone without too much concern that they wouldn't like it, unless they hate quilts (still looks wrong) a lot.

RATING: 9
This is a polished design that integrates a spatial puzzle (like Tetris or Ubongo), a light economic element, and a time track system into a 2-player abstract that is very pleasant to play.   It's not overly thinky, even though there is zero luck.   The pieces are not evenly costed, and can be quite situational, plus you can only purchase from the next 3.  So, while there is some look-ahead, the AP is not severe.   Not to mention, they totally got the look of the game correct.   Very impressed with this one.

RATING: 8.5
I make this ranking before having played either Feast for Odin or Barenpark. Back when Patchwork was the only game to experiment with the idea of filling a board with various sized tetrisy pieces, I was enamored. Careful planning, both on when to execute certain purchases and where to place them, is pivotal to success and there's a strong satisfaction to nearly completing the board (I've not yet seen anyone pull off a full board.)

Now I need to see how I find these new-comers. If Barenpark or Feast for Odin prove better games than Patchwork, then I'll likely see Patchwork drop a couple points - whereas, if Patchwork still proves my preferred game in this genre, I'll be pumping it up a little bit.

RATING: 8
I was skeptical when I first saw pictures of Patchwork. Tetris-esque pieces and a quilting theme... yeah. It has lovely graphic design, but so did Nika. After numerous positive comments from Geekbuddies and BGG in general, I decided to check it out. I was very pleasantly surprised. Normally, I actively dislike 2-player abstracts with many permutations to churn. After setup, this is a perfect information abstract, and while you do need to churn some permutations, it doesn't feel as weighed down to me in this game compared to Chess and similar games. I think it has to do with the fact that you don't have many different pieces to consider moving. It's just the common piece and your own piece. Even when pondering various moves, this game still plays pretty quickly. There are many layers to your decision with regards to time, income, shapes, the common pawn positioning, time-track positioning. It's just pretty lovely. The theme and puzzley nature should make it appealing for couples.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[b]Rating based on - 200+ plays, 2 player, Android app[/b]
I avoided this game for quite a long time because of the theme, but then I kept hearing it being mentioned a lot as a really good abstract (and who can resist a really good abstract?) so I got the app. Patchwork is basically a spatial reasoning abstract strategy economic puzzle that is dressed in pretty pieces. It uses the Time Track mechanism as in Thebes and Glen More so the person in the last position on the track always goes first. You need to balance your need for income (buttons), with the necessity to also cover your board almost completely or risk the penalty for uncovered spaces. Usually the patches with the most buttons don't cover as many spaces as larger button-less patches (although there are certain exceptions) so there are certain tricky decisions to be made with those, and also fitting the patches you choose with the others already on your board.

At first I thought there was a quite high element of luck because my win rate was about 50% and I thought it depended upon the patches available to me. It turns out there is a bit more than that involved. Now that I have more experience and over 100 wins, I kind of grok the strategy. A more experienced player will usually crush a newbie and there is a guy who played over 300 games and lost only 20. Now that is IMPRESSIVE! Some people have a knack for both being able to present you with crap options on your turn, and make a garden of roses out of it if those same options are presented to them on their turn. The 7x7 bonus I look at as a catch up mechanism for the person with the least buttons. However, in general I tend to see the person with the button lead getting that bonus as well. If that happens it's a surety that person will win. Games are more fun for me if it's a tight close race to the end. The foregone conclusion is disappointing.

It's a nice little challenge and after playing on the app I can say I definitely will not be getting a hard copy.
1. Due to the asynchronous nature of play I can play a few minutes here and there whenever I get a chance,
2. I can run several games at a time with many different opponents,
3. The interface is beautiful and the patches graphics change from game to game,
4. Games are quick and interesting, if a bit dry and mathy
5. But most of all...The other half is not that good at spatial reasoning and while the game is cute and clever, it just doesn't offer enough to enter it in the collection.
[b]Status: KEEPER (for now)[/b]

RATING: 9
I played with an experienced player and although I had a good score on my 2nd game, was still beaten soundly.  I was perplexed how I lost, something that usually isn't difficult to evaluate.  I had the same number of buttons, I managed to get more turns, I had nearly the same number of empty spaces (negative points), and gained my share of filler tiles.  I didn't get the free tile, nor the bonus tile, but that didn't account for all of the difference.  The winner told me she goes after the biggest tiles.  True, but I think obtaining lots of buttons early is the primary key, so you receive money more times for the same buttons, since money wins the game.  Just 1 or 2 lower payouts early on could lose the game.  

Pluses: Planning ahead strategy, spatial relationships, easy rules, quick setup, half hour filler game, interesting. The game itself is more attractive than the dull looking box.

Cons:  the puzzle pieces don't always fit together well so there is a little fear of damaging the pieces.  Hard to catch someone with a good start.

Especially addictive if you like puzzles.  Many of the pieces are identical to Cathedral & Blokus ones.  Great kids game.

After playing this game a few times, raised my rating.  This is a much greater strategic game than I had realized with the first play.  Timing, a specific kind of planning ahead, turns out to be a huge  an important part of this game.  The fourth game turned into a real brain burner.

Raising rating again after 11 plays to 9.  T

he BGG game weight is rated at 1.70.  Because of the advanced strategy in such a deceptively simple game, I think the weight should be a 3.5.

RATING: 9.5
Patchwork continues to impress me with how easy it is to play and how deep it can be. It never gets too much past a tactical level of planning, but every one of those decisions is equally agonizing and satisfying. A well-played game is also incredibly satisfying as you gradually patch up every open spot on your board. Those things plus an ideal length combine to make Patchwork one of my top 5 two player games, and one of my top 25 overall. Highly recommended!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
It's a really nice set of mechanisms. I love the time track, it's one of my favourite mechanisms. The patch puzzle is fun, but somewhat banal at times since you only ever have at most 3 patches to choose from and some of those you may not be able to afford. The button economy works, but it's so obvious that buttons on patches are super-imortant, especially early in the game, that all other patches (and there's plenty of them) become practically worthless for at least the first half of the game. This combined with only 3 choices of patches, of which you can't always afford all, means that the game is too void of hard decisions to be interesting to me. You can argue that how you place your patches is an interesting decision, but because of the race to 7x7 it's a solid strategy to just build from one corner and outwards. There's also the choice of not picking a piece, but that's usually bad, not very fun and usually something you're forced to do, meaning that it's no choice at all. 

I also have a problem with the 7x7 bonus. It's good that there's some incentive to make a neat and hole-less quilt but the 14 button swing it generates practically guarantees victory, especially with 2 players of equal skill.

In conclusion, I liked the game, but I wanted to like it much more. It's held back by some issues that I'm not sure are fixable, it's simply not made to be the game I wanted it to be.

RATING: 10
A wonderful combination of different decisions: puzzling as you fit patches into your quilt, timing your purchases in relation to your income, and balancing the tradeoffs between patch size/shape, income potential, button cost and time cost. Supremely enjoyable to play.

A favorite of my my 4 y.o. who started playing when she was 3.5. She enjoys making her quilt and can beat me on occasion, only needing assistance to make sure she doesn't forget to take income, move her marker on the time track, make change, etc. Younger children can definitely play this game!

RATING: 7
Will frequently grab this as a game to travel with. Though it takes up a surprisingly large amount of space. Just doesn't seem to have enough depth for me to rank it among the best 2p games. It seems relatively easy to calculate the 'value' of each tile. Taking tiles that have buttons on them early is obvious. Then you switch to tiles that cover more spaces later on. This arc is the same from play to play. The game is all in the timing of those choices.

Best played ruthlessly. Often, denying your opponent a great play is more important than taking a good play for yourself.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Patchwork is a great little Lofi game: great rulest-to-depth-ratio. Not only is it an aesthetic treat (i.e., it's quirky and cute), it also offers a great series of small yet significant choices around six criteria which Ben Draper outlines so clearly in his comments:
[q=BennyD]1) Button cost, i.e. VP cost
2) Time cost, i.e. finite resource equal between players
3) Tempo cost, i.e. actions given up to the other player in order to do this particular action
4) Button gain, i.e. regular source of VPs which rewards early investment
5) Spatial coverage, i.e. one time VP gains
6) Shape irregularity, i.e. loss of chance at bonus VPs and/or potential spatial coverage
[/q]
The time cost is brilliant (although we've seen it elsewhere, e.g., [thing=12681][/thing]), it gives a great tempo and rythm to how and what you pick, above and beyond the immediate "how much does it cost, how much space does it cover, and what does it provide in terms of later economy" questions. This can be especially pleasureful in handing off control when the choices aren't terribly hot!

The spatial logic required of the patchworking process means that your ability to valuate the other components is directly linked to your ability (and/or desire) to add the particular shape to your board. This makes and breaks the "engine" part of the game and adds a great additional component to what is otherwise an economic tug-of-war without it muddying the clean and simple design.

Overall, Rosenberg has yet another hit on his hands which begs the question: now why doesn't he design a big game with this Lofi approach? :)

A clever, clever little two player game.

RATING: 7
Uwe Rosneberg újabb kétszemélyes kisdobozos játéka. Nem annyira mély mint a LeHavre és az Agricola kétszemélyes verziói, de a barátnőmet pont a témája ragadta meg nagyon. Tetrisből ismert alakzatú mintákat rakunk ki a pálya köré majd egy bábuval 1-3 lépést megtéve elvehetünk egy nekünk megfelelő alakzatot és lehelyezni a táblánkra. Az alakzatokért gombokkal fizetünk. De az alakzatok nem csak gombba, hanem időbe is kerülnek, amit a középső táblán lépjük le. Ha ott gombos mezőket lépünk át, akkor megkapjuk azokat a gombokat, amelyek az alakzatokon láthatók. Cél minél kevesebb hiánnyal lefedni a táblánkat. 

Egyszerű, szórakoztató játék, amelyben egyszerre kell az idővel és a gombokkal gazdálkodnunk.

RATING: 8
1.每人起始5元
2.從2元1時間板塊左方開始
3.兩個動作:
a.買指示物接下來三個拼圖其中一個，付錢跟移動時間
#當移動時間經過鈕扣時，獲得收入(計算自己圖板的鈕扣數)
#經過補丁可以拿取，須馬上拚
b.Pass購買，移動自己指示物到對手前面一格，每走一格拿一元。
4.在後面的玩家永遠先動作，重疊以上面優先
5.完成7x7板塊，可以拿取Bonus 7元
6.遊戲最後比金錢，每個沒完成空格一個扣2元。

RATING: 7.5
Two-players game very light, very neat, easy to explain and to play and with a very decent level of strategy. The focus of the game is to complete a 9x9 board with fabric of kind of Tetris pieces. One of the points of the game is to decide whether to try to be the first player in covering a 7x7 shape, probably leaving many empty spots on the board and being penalized for that, or trying to cover as much surface as possible.
Positive:
1. Easy to play
2. Quick to learn
3. Good level of strategy
4. Can be played for any type of player
Negative:
1. Only 2 player game
2. I am not sure about the replayability of the game

RATING: 7
A nice little filler suitable for Family, Gateway and maybe Couple play, super EASY to learn like 2 minutes (read good for kids too), and done in about 30 mins. 

I was hoping for a little more ooomph to it from seeing some of the buzz, there is a little for sure and more than it seems at first blush but not really enough to get it fully out of filler territory for me (close!). I would likely choose Gric All Creatures most times over this for a 2 player 30 min game, or a pile of others but it should have enough to keep your interest with the spacial and engine aspects and then the movement and time track juggling and there is fairly good control with 2 players only. Theme is cute but wafer-thin. 

Sidenotes - Funny that POF experience was relevant here in the "Tetris" board building aspect. I was a little surprised that moving 3 spaces was not more expensive than moving 1 when buying things, it might have added a slight tactical element and point to ponder when making your moves. Also wondered why someone could NOT choose how many spaces to move when doing this for money on timetrack , instead they had to move enough to pass opponent (both of these might have been for simplicity or other reasons or combo of those)

RATING: 8.4
Bokkensprong 16/10/15 met Sander en ik. Doel: elk op zijn eigen vierkante rasterbordje een patchwork maken van tetris-achtige stukken, en zo knopen (=geld=punten) verdienen. De stukjes liggen uitgestald in een grote cirkel; de eerste drie na de pion zijn te koop voor tijdstappen + knopen. Extra knopen zijn te verdienen voor een volledig dicht patchwork. Knopen worden afgetrokken voor elk leeg rastervakje. Tof familiespelletje voor twee.

Gekregen voor 41e verjaardag van Anneken :)

RATING: 8
Patchwork can be described as tactical, two-player, turn-based Tetris with two-currencies, time and money.

That description makes me drool.

Fortunately, the game delivers on this promise. My only complaint is that, while the game is easy to learn, it takes a few games to get good at putting the puzzle pieces together and understanding how to efficiently use the game's currencies. A veteran player will crush a new player, which might be a turn off for some (especially with a game of this complexity).

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
2015-03-18

Initial Rating: 5.0 (March 2015)

So far, I have liked every Rosenberg game I have played, but I was disappointed in Patchwork, I was expecting a heavier game from him.

The game is exceedingly simple with only two actions to choose from each turn, and in many turns you don’t have to choose which one to play because one action will be unavailable. I don’t like the theme, but it is a, somewhat, novel one. 

On the good side, the game is gorgeous and play very fast (its best feature). I think it can be a good family game.

Bottom line, I feel the game is very obvious and shallow but I could be wrong. I don’t mind playing light games but they have to offer interesting decisions and so far I haven’t seen them in Patchwork. I need to play it again to see if I’m wrong but for now I’m leaning towards getting rid of the game. My GF liked the game.

Current Rating: 5.0

RATING: 7
The rules are very simple while still creating a thoughtful and fun experience. It loses points for me because it's 2p only, which means I won't get a chance to play it very often. It's also a touch lighter than I would like.

[b]Time to pay the price[/b]
I love time tracks. I first encountered that mechanism in Thebes. It serves elegantly as both an action point system and a turn order track. Patchwork adds icons to the time track that when passed trigger income for the player passing them. The multi-use aspect of the track is very appealing and adds some decisions and tension to the game.

RATING: 8
Brillant in its simplicity. The tradeoff decisions between buying an expensive tile now for higher payout later or a cheaper tile for more alternatives in the short term, weighing a positional advantage on the player board vs. the benefit of a needed patch and evaluating this vs. potentially leaving a good choice for your opponent are challenging and often non-trivial.

Patchwork even functions thematically despite its abstract nature. While it initially looks like Tetris, the puzzle part is the least important. Too bad that my girlfriend is annoyed after two massive defeats. Too much thought involved for casual enjoyment?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A good, ingenious, slightly cerebral, but unexciting economic game with a Tetris component. It’s easy to teach, set up and play. 

Each player has to accumulate buttons to spend on pieces that both fit into the Tetris shape and let them earn more buttons. At the same time, each player has to judge how best to manoeuvre on a timeline that contains additional bonus pieces. 

It’s a puzzle with three things to organise - trying to buy the most advantageous piece for yourself while denying your opponent too many good choices, fitting pieces together in an intelligent way, and advancing cleverly on a time-line. 

While there’s no conflict between the players, there’s also no social interaction. The exchanges during the game tend to be “I think I’ll buy this piece…” and that’s about it.

Managing button income and time spent on various pieces is where the interesting gameplay stems from.  The mechanism of the last player taking as many turns as they can/want until they pass the first player on the time track is also quite interesting.  Fun little abstract game that plays in about 15-20 minutes.

RATING: 6
Rated 5 after one play:

tl;dr version: Very light game for casual gamers.

For any gamer, this is way too simple.  I watched two friends play and I feel like I had the optimal strategy down in a couple of minutes.

I then proceeded to destroy the previous winner (who had some experience playing the game) in my first match by a score of 34 to something like 10.  Now, she's a casual gamer, so I wasn't surprised, and here lies the problem.

If you play against another good player, I imagine that there can be a lot of very clever moves that you can do to screw your opponent over and/or set yourself up for future plays.  However, I can't imagine two gamers playing this game and having a ton of fun doing it.  I certainly can't.

Casual players might enjoy trying to fill up their boards the best they can, and scoring anywhere between -20 and +20 points.

But the real depth of the game comes from playing with gamers who will count everything, maximize their investments and set up future plays to get (or steal) the needed patches.

So it's either a (not very) deep game that gamers won't enjoy that much, or a game casual gamers might enjoy without experiencing its full potential.

Uwe fans are very likely to be disappointed.  The game is targeting a completely different audience, and while that's OK, this is information that's needed before purchasing the game.

---

After about 20 plays:

I kept playing at work (because we get down time in which there's little to do).  I enjoy the game quite a bit more, but not enough to play it outside of work.

There is quite a bit of challenge from setting up future plays that's quite enjoyable for me.  The game is still pretty light, but it's better than I originally thought. 

Counting the tiles' worth is annoying.  It's simple math, but it's quite repetitive.

RATING: 9
I struggle a little bit to rate this one a 9 as I'm not sure it fully deserves its current spot as the #1 Abstract game.  To abstract game fans it likely isn't but it's immense draw comes from the rest of us who primarily play other types of games.  In that regard it is definitely one of our favorite abstracts in that it plays pretty quickly yet has very satisfying decision making.  I am a big fan of games that employ the time tracking game mechanic and this is likely a lot of people's first exposure to it (which may have resulted in the game being rated higher than it might otherwise have been, not sure).  I remember similar time mechanics in everything from Sun, Sea and Sand to FFG's Horus Heresy.  The way it is used in Patchwork is definitely NOT the most creative use of the mechanic however it may well be the BEST use of it in combination with the others as the whole game is basically more-or-less managing button income vs tetris like board space coverage vs cost in time.  Perhaps its best accomplishment though is in providing a filler level game that doesn't seem very random at all.  Still its not perfect and if I had to define its one point loss from a perfect 10 myself I would go with the one random element that is within the game which is the order the tiles are layed out in.  It can occur through no fault of the players that there are 3 extremely expensive tiles all in a row such that there is no valid move but for both players to pass and take 2 buttons each several turns in a row until one can afford one (This could even happen as a starting setup on turn 1).  There is another version of this where the game can stall out near the end because the next 3 tiles have no valid placement for either player even though scores of other tiles beyond those would be valid.  Fortunately neither situation happens which much frequency.  You could easily argue the theme is pasted on, but for the weight of the game I'd say it actually comes across pretty good and is likely part of the reason for its success vs. just having been red and blue pieces or something to that effect.  I've rarely given my wife games as presents in the past, but took a chance with this one.  Right now it is still her favorite game.

[size=12][b]Top 200 board games list[/b][/size]

[size=12][b]Why I like Patchwork[/b][/size]
+ I like the mechanics
+ There is decent player involvement
+ The game has decent replayability
+ The game is easy to teach
+ The game is short
+ The game requires meaningful decisions to win the game. 

[size=12][b]Why I dislike Patchwork:[/b][/size]
- I wish the game had more decisions to make. I think I'd rather pick from a pool of tiles than have to grab whatever is three spaces from my pawn. I hope to compare and contrast Patchwork with Barenpark.
- I prefer other two player games

RATING: N/A
In Patchwork, two players compete to build the most aesthetic (and high-scoring) patchwork quilt on a personal 9x9 game board. To start play, lay out all of the patches at random in a circle and place a marker directly clockwise of the 2-1 patch. Each player takes five buttons — the currency/points in the game — and someone is chosen as the start player.

RATING: 7.2
Is it novel as many users state? No, it isn't, it's more like Uwe Rosenberg (the designer of some famous games where you buy tiles to place them on your personal boards to produce and also to cover negative scoring spaces) reworking Reiner Knizia in his style.
Is it a problem? Oh no, it isn't. It's a fine game; I must admit the result is more interesting than those Knizias. And the Patchwork look and 'theme' is really fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
[2016.Feb.29] This short, 2-player puzzle-like abstract is easily approachable by both gamers and non-gamers alike. With only 2 possible actions each player turn, there's not much heavy thinking required. The trickiest part is deciding how to place your acquired puzzle... er, I mean quilt piece. It is a nice addition to almost any collection. I hope your [i]Patchwork[/i] quilt isn't as moth-eaten as mine typically turn out to be.

RATING: 7
Ein reines 2-Personen Spiel, wenn sich die Gelegenheit mal ergibt ;).
Im Kreis liegen Flicken aus, die wir in unseren Teppich einbauen möchten. Wer an der Reihe ist nimmt sich eines der drei nächsten Flicken, näht es in seinen Flickenteppich ein und bezahlt Knöpfe und Zeit auf einer Zeitleiste. Es ist immer derjenige Spieler dran, der bis dato weniger Zeit ausgegeben hat, somit können multiple Züge entstehen, wenn ein Spieler sehr "Zeitteure" Plättchen erwirbt und der andere dagegen "günstige". Auf dieser Zeitleiste gibt es immer wieder einzelne Bereiche, die beim Überschreiten eine Knöpfe-Ausschüttung hervorrufen. Die sind zwingend notwendig um flüssig zu bleiben, denn wer zu wenig Knöpfe hat muss "aussetzten" und erhält dadurch ein paar Knöpfe, verschenkt aber seinen Zug. Sobald die Zeitsteine das Ende des Tracks erreichen endet das Spiel und wer jetzt mehr Knöpfe hat gewinnt.
Mir hat das Spiel in den ersten Partien nur mäßig gefallen, es wurde aber mit der Zeit immer besser, bis ich es mir sogar selbst gekauft habe. Jetzt spiele ich es sehr gerne.

RATING: 9
[b]Patchwork is a thoughtful puzzler of acquiring and placing tiles stitched together with a delightfully approachable theme.[/b]
r{[i]I found this game to be surprisingly good, so much so that I bought it immediately after having played it once.[/i]}r

SYNOPSIS
Two players race to efficiently piece together a quilt with Tetris-like patch work shapes purchased using buttons as currency which are acquired over time. Quilts are judged for missing patches with poor results subtracting from one's score of accumulated buttons.

COMMENTS
Rosenberg's game excels at what he sets out to do with his design which is first to create a tight resource market in acquiring pieces of patchwork and second to force you to solve a spatial puzzle in placing your pieces to shape a quilt.

PROS+, CONS- & NOTES*
+ It's a bit of a brain burner that I admire for how well it plays.
+ Simple and easily understood rules paired with a clever button acquisition and time keeping main board make for a (dare I say it) elegant game.
* Simple oval set up of patch work pieces nicely accommodates their loose storage in box.

RATING: 7
Rosenberg is best known for games in which you have to build a farm by first gathering enough quanta to assemble an atom, then making atoms into elements, and so on, until you have a pig or a rock. But once he made games like Bohnanza and Klunker. 

Patchwork is a game that can be as casual or cutthroat as you want (within reason -- it's not Diplomacy or anything). At first it seems like you don't have enough buttons to even make decisions, but before long you have options to weigh, and can even get tricky about it. A good time, and a welcome change of pace.

RATING: 7.5
This fascinating little two-player game is evidence of the conceptual genius of Uwe Rosenberg.  On its face, it’s an abstract strategy game about making a patchwork quilt, but the hook here is that it’s really about five games in one:  strategy, time track, puzzle game, resource management, and tile placement are all represented in Patchwork to one degree or another.  There’s even a bit of card-counting/spatial relations.  What’s amazing is that it all works!

A cute theme (and another non-violent one, for those of you who care) and decent artwork, though nothing will blow you away. It’s a small thing, but the one big headache is that at the start of the game, the patch pieces take up a ton of space.  Otherwise, it’s a remarkably competitive, surprisingly tense game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Probably the best 2-player game I've come across yet.  In a basic sense, I would describe it as Tetris the board game, though it goes beyond that.  Yes, you have normal bisymmetrical shapes (quilt patterns) to lay out on your quilt (your board) but you also have these oblong shapes/patterns that can really mess things up for you.  Using buttons as currency to purchase the quilt patterns, there is a fun strategy involved of not overspending, making sure you don't advance too far, too fast on the time track and also making sure you don't place your patterns in such a way where you paint yourself into a corner.  I absolutely love this very clever game.

RATING: 7
Tetris with an economic engine, this game has a very simple ruleset yet is quite brain-burny. Since you use almost all the tiles every game this rating is a bit tentative as I am unsure of its replayability, but it is quite possible that the order of the tiles matter a lot and a master of this game could potentially chain tile combinations to perfectly fill up their board without empty spaces in between. Also it appears to be pretty important to make sure you choose tiles so that you cross the button icons; otherwise you will be stuck with no buttons to buy tiles on your subsequent turns.

RATING: 9
A simple two player game where you have a series of tetris-like shapes played out in circle.  You can buy one of the next 1 to 3 of them or gain buttons by moving one past your opponent.  The object is to fill up a 9x9 grid and gain as many buttons as you can.  Any unfilled spaces reduce your button count.  Buttons are money and victory points.  The game is much deeper than it appears on the surface but plays quickly and I find it very fun.  Very family friendly and good for kids and adults.  Uwe Rosenberg is brilliant.

Am Spielende gewinnt also der Spieler mit den meisten Knöpfen abzüglich zweier Knöpfe für jedes nicht abgedeckte Feld seines Tableaus.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
There's a wealth of decisions generated from a quirky mixture of Tetris and a very basic economy engine, and on top you get an excellent graphics implementation of the 'theme', for lack of a better word - shiny buttons, bright patterns on your quilt pieces, and non-intrusive game information.

After a single play, it's hard to judge the depth of any game, but I suspect that Patchwork has quite a lot of planning to offer once you start to pay attention to the needs of your opponent as well as to your own. Never thought I would consider adding another two-player abstract to our collection, but this one surely has me tempted ...

RATING: 9
Nifty little two-player game, a theme I've never seen before (quilting), and some really interesting "double economies": You spend your victory points to do things, and time is also a currency.﻿

It's pleasant to play. That's not damning it with faint praise: It's a genuinely pleasant experience, somehow relaxing despite the fact that every turn is full of tough decisions.

It has an interesting rhythm to it, too, with the pace depending on a wide range of variables that change every turn.

You are not so much aggressive in this game as passive-aggressive.

RATING: 9

Once you've gotten a few games under your belt, check out the strategy article that talks about button rates to take your game to the next level.

RATING: 8
I was skeptical at first. I hate tetris, and quilting is for girls...But after i set my pride aside and played this game, this game is incredible. I love the engine building mechanic of buying the pieces that produce more buttons for you when you hit a scoring round. Bonus patches if you're the first to reach a spot on the time track are awesome. But you have to weigh that with taking your time and buying the pieces that give you the most for your money, and really utilizing the time track to your advantage. Sometimes being behind the other player is better so you can string together a combo of good pieces. Quite a nice balance between getting the button pieces that subsequently speed you along on the time track faster than you'd like, with buying the value pieces that fill up your quilt more. Great balance. I like how the token skips pieces and works its way back around in a circle. Put your pride away and give this game a try, it's incredible. My new favorite two player game.

RATING: 9
Fun
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.3
Very simple game you can play almost right away. 

Trying to fit every patch on your board, getting that 7x7 patchwork bonus, trying to hamper the opponent in getting certainpieces, optimising your time and button-income and trying to get multiple turns before the other goes again. Trying to be on top of your opponent on the time-track is a very powerful move.

Need to play it more, but I like it already after the first play.

With promo: real buttons and neutral 'pawn'.

Edit: great 'filler' type of game with a jigsaw puzzle mechanic. It's a very attractive game with the right theme and short playing time. The 7x7 bonus isn't Always necessary. Try to go for big tiles with lots of buttons! And mind the end of the time track: goign to fast will net you a lot of holes in your patchwork!

I really love this adorable game.

Edit2: one minor thing. The only incentive to make a 'beautiful' patchwork is the 7x7 tile. If you manage to make a much larger block (which is quite a feat), it isn't rewarded. Trying to fit in the 'best' piece (and then probably leaving some open spaces) rewards more points.

RATING: 8
A game about buying and placing patches. A patch is a polyomino - it has a size (squares covered), a shape (a square, a line, a cube, a wierd looking thing), two costs (price and time), and a income value (represented by the number of buttons on the tile). On purchase you pay, take and place the patch on your personal "Quilt", then move your marker, and if you're still behind your opposition you get to go again. A true combinatorial game - everything is visible from the get go, but the feel is completely different to what those games typically tend to give.

Turns out juggling tetris pieces in your head, trying to craft a plan for your next couple of moves, knowing your opponent is doing the same and also trying to do the best to screw you, is bloody hard! In a great fun and tense way that allows you to feel so clever when you get it right, and the "Oh bloody hell..." dismay and frustration when you realise that no, those two don't fit there, and no, you didn't have enough to purchase that so now you have to pass.

Excellent and tight. It's a game you can grow with, and I feel that the strategic space opens up one level of understanding at the time - you start considering not just your own board, but really more your opponents. It's not just both players building their patch in peace and quiet, no it's both players trying to scrape together a patch while your opponent is out with scissors trying to cut yours up and you are trying to set his/hers on fire.

My verdict: Easy to get to the table and a great couple game, or just a great game for anyone really!

RATING: 7

RATING: 8.28
[b][url=https://boardgamegeek.com/article/17381909]Patchwork First Impressions[/b][/url]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a really neat two player game. You are working to make a quilt by buying tetris-inspired swatch pieces. Each piece costs some kind of combination of time and buttons, for each time it costs the player moves their marker along the track, and whoever is furthest behind gets to play next. Each time a marker crosses a button, the player receives an income of buttons according to how many buttons are on their quilt at the time, each time a player passes they receive a button for each space they have to move along the time track, and whenever a player piece passes one of the single square swatch pieces on the track, they immediately adds it to their quilt. The game ends when both players reach the end of the time track, and they score according to the amount of buttons they have earned, deduct two points for each open space in their quilt and if the player managed to earn the 7x7 bonus tile for being the first to complete a 7x7 grid on their quilt they earn another 7 bonus points.

This is a simple to teach, but also highly strategic game, really recommend it.

Got this to play with wife and extended family. Bought this for the memorial week family reunion and this easily got the most plays (even more than cribbage, which is saying something with a card playing family). My mother and older sister played it 5 times while we watched a movie. It was quick enough that people watching it played could call "next" and get in a game. Update: This is one of my go to games to bring to things. It is guaranteed to get played. My mother-in-law actually borrows it every other week to play with her friends and husband. Will have to get her a copy.

Update 2.0: Got mother in law a copy for Christmas. Now I can keep my copy at the house. This game is quick enough that it sees lots of play and simple enough that it can be taught to anyone. Really enjoy it.

Update 3.0: I think the reason this has so much staying power for me, is that it is one of the few games that I can play with anyone of any skill level and still enjoy the game. Most games that are friendly to non-gamers aren't very enjoyable for me.

RATING: 9
Cannot say enough about how impressed I am with this great 2-player!  Plenty of depth and hard decisions that encourage you to think many turns in advance, also forcing you to consider what you may be leaving for your opponent.  Yet the gameplay is so simple and light, easy to teach.  One of my wife's favorites (and mine if I'm looking for a shorter game)!  It's pretty quick, and a small package to boot!  A very non-threatening, relaxed, but still fulfilling gaming experience. Top-notch!  Only thing keeping me from rating it higher is for such a small game, the initial set-up takes up more room than you'd expect on a table.  But it gets smaller as the game goes on.  Not a big issue by any means, and it really isn't that much room.  And we'll see how much longevity it has (but I think that it'll last us quite a long time).

RATING: 7
Kvázi egy modern tetrisz, egyedi szabályokkal. Kifejezetten érdekes, hogy nem csak az ár, hanem az idő is tényező a foltok varrásánál, ami miatt még jobban lehet benne taktikázni.

A játék végén elég erős a bevarratlan mezők utáni 2 pont levonás mezőnként, simán lehet 0 pont alá is menni emiatt.

Csak két játékos játszhatja (van mondjuk nem hivatalos "szóló" mód is), amit mondjuk lehetett volna akár 3-4-re is növelni több folttal és plusz játékos táblákkal. Igaz, akkor a foltok már nem biztos, hogy elférnének egy átlagos méretű asztalon...

Mivel túl sok interakció nincs a két játékos között (konkrétan csak annyi, hogy a kinézett foltot elveheti előlünk az ellenfél, ha ő van körön), ezért egyedül ez hozható fel neki még negatívumnak.

Egyébként szórakoztató, könnyed taktikai játék, egyszerű szabályokkal, belépő szintnek tökéletes, minőségi játékelemekkel.

UPDATE: Megvettem az android appját is, az esseni akcióban. Kiválóan megcsinálták, visszaadja a játék hangulatát, jól kezelhető és online játék mellett van lehetőség AI ellen is játszani (legnehezebb ellenfél ellen kifejezetten esélytelen nyerni).

RATING: 7
An amazingly fun game to play. By far the most richly rewarding 2-player filler game I've played. Beautiful in its simplicity, but with a surprising amount of depth, although I suspect that will diminish somewhat after more plays. 

I bought this specifically to play with my wife, hoping it would provide something a little deeper and more engaging than just going through the motions of yet another play of Ticket To Ride, Qwirkle, or Lost Cities. We've been badly in need of a game to bridge the gap between my desire for something deeper and less samey than the above-mentioned games, and her distaste for long, complex games. Patchwork is (at least for now) the perfect compromise.

Update: Downgraded from 9 to 7. It's still a good game, but once you work out the formula for figuring out which tiles give the biggest bang for the buck (in terms of both time and buttons) and you start to memorize which tiles are good and which are bad, then the game gets a lot less interesting, and the choices become more obvious.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
An underwhelming game from my favorite designer.  There are 3 things to consider: getting buttons, filling spaces and managing time.  None of these things is really at odds with any other, so there is very little tension.  As one of your first few moves, you may need to advance on the time track to get an injection of buttons, but after that you always want to buy swatches:  so almost all of the game consists of picking one of the 3 available swatches.  Which one do you pick?  (1) The one with the most buttons, (2) The biggest, (3) The one you can afford.  You repeat this simple heuristic for the whole game.

Patchwork von Uwe Rosenberg ist ein eingängiges 2-Personen Spiel mit einem sehr ungewöhnlichen Thema. Die Spieler versuchen aus Stoffteilen einen hübschen Flickenteppich anzufertigen. Die Spielmechanik ist so genial wie simpel: Alle Stoffflicken werden in einem großen Kreis angeordnet. An einer bestimmten Stelle, steht ein Meeple und nur die 3 Flicken, die vor dem Meeple liegen, dürfen erworben werden. Zahlen müssen die Spieler mit Knöpfen und Zeit und so rücken sie auf dem kleinen Spielbrett, mehrere Felder nach vorne. Die Flickenteile haben die Form von Tetrissteinen und müssen nun geschickt auf dem eigenen Teppich "platziert" werden. Ein einfaches Spiel für zwischendurch, mit einem netten Thema und liebevollen Design.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.4
Probably the most elegant 2-player game I've played. Rules are simple but there is a lot you can strategize. Good players definitely fill their boards more often than new players. What I have also found out, this game is great with players who don't normally play boardgames. Patchwork can be played completely ignoring your opponent which is easier for a newer player. However, good player can do a lot of thinking ahead according to your opponents moves.

Patchwork also has a very elegant time mechanic which I simply love. It feels natural after a while and it is a new and thematic mechanic. 

Overall, a great 2-player game. There is also very good mobile version of this game which includes asymmetric online play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.9
Video Review - https://youtu.be/sE3FwDcEzpg

Patchwork is a two player tile laying game based around making your own quilt. But don't let the theme put your off. This is an excellent quick game with plenty of decisions to make. Players are seeking to finish the game with the least gaps in their quilt (-2 for each one) and the most buttons (1 for each one) in their collection. They achieve this by using buttons to buy patches which they place on their quilt but also cause their counter to move further along the time track. It is a real balance between moving and cost as sometimes you won't want to move that far as it gives your opponent more choice. At various points you earn more buttons or a single square patch, and there is also a bonus if you are first to make a 7 by 7 square. Turns are not taken in order but instead the player furthest behind on the time track plays next. This gives you an opportunity to chain moves together. On your turn you can buy and play a patch, or move in front of the other player taking an amount of buttons for the spaces moved. Brilliant and simple.

RATING: 7
Very impressed by this game. Has a very easy barrier to entry, but the ceiling for doing well is very, very high. Games of this are tense, and every move you make could make or break the game for you. It's kind of an oddity, because while the rules are extremely simple, the amount of thought needed to play well at this game is far above what you'd expect a 2-player filler game to have. I'm not normally a fan of Rosenburg's games, but this one was a pleasant surprise for me. I couldn't care less about the theme, but the gameplay is solid, fun, and addictive.

UPDATE: I've lowered my rating slightly due to burnout. The game is still fun, but I'm not sure there is a ton left to explore for me personally.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Patchwork plays like a beautiful blend of Tetris and Euro resource management. On one hand, you need to plan your economy, so that you have a steady income to purchase tiles for. On the other hand, you need to plan your board so that the pieces fit without holes.

To accomplish this, Uwe has blended some simple mechanics into an excellent whole where no decision is given. Do you want to advance slowly on the tile track to buy as many big tiles as possible or fast to pick up those small free tiles awarded to the first to reach them? Is it better to choose a good tile for yourself or leave a bad tile for your opponent? And what is a "good tile" given that you have to consider its shape, cost, time and future income?

My only concern is that the opening moves can be forced if most of the early tiles are too expensive but it may also be because I don't handle the opening well yet.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I'm skeptical of reviews, especially when they all say the same thing: "High intensity" on a quilting game?! But then I tried it. Dude. Duuuuuuude. That is some high intensity gameplay. We actually had to devise a "quilt bag" from which to draw the tiles and use a d20 to randomize which the actual start tile would be, counting *from* the smallest/start marker, to avoid any appearance of loading advantage. For such a simple-looking game (like, I was thinking, how hard is Tetris when you don't have to insert blocks on a timer, really?) it actually has several strategy routes, none of which appear to work all the way through, so you have to improvise and combine; you want to cover all your squares, but you need buttons to get pieces, but neither of these per-piece qualities are linked to the time factor, so the decision tree rapidly turns into a decision graphing calculator if you're a competitive freak like me, or just a delightful smorgasbord of possibilities with the occasional gotcha or big cash-in if you're playing it as a lighter weight game. Perfect for two whiling away an afternoon or for one gamer to draw one normal over to the cardboard side; Rosenberg knocks this one out of the park.

RATING: 8
This is a lovely little head-to-head game about making a quilt. It's almost too twee to get on board with at first; you use buttons for currency and try not to have any holes in your blanket. I mean... really. But there is something wonderfully nice about this game. The 'catch-up' mechanic does a good job of keeping the game competitive (it's very hard for a clear winner to emerge until the end) and it's a solid little mix-up of resource management and planning. Designed specifically for two players, it's a very simple game which can be learned quickly and definitely worth the twenty minutes it takes to play. It's just... so... twee.

RATING: 9.1
Great 2-player game, nice and simple in a small box.  Quick to learn and play with endless possibilities.  I bought a cheaper Greek version because there are no words on the pieces and you can download the simple rules by Googling for a PDF.  4-player variant by the same designer is Cottage Garden.

You basically pay for tetris pieces to fit on your own grid with each piece either: costing a lot, or moving you forward a lot, or having many buttons that earn you points.  There don't seem to be large pieces with point scoring buttons on that move you on 1 or 2 spaces and cost little, but it does make you wonder if there is a rough formula to follow - I tend not to pay much more than 3 1/2 per button and avoid big moves.

RATING: 7
I'm gonna be honest I did not like this game at all the first few times we played it. I found the game to be way too casual, a bit boring and some aspects of the game very very pointless, so Patchwork just gathered dust on my little shelf. I never understood why this game was so popular. I came to a point where I started looking for possible trades. One day I decided to take this game out and give it another chance. We looked at the rules again and realised we have played it completely wrong before. We opened up Netflix on the side and casually played the game while rewatching Friends. Perfect. Absolutely brilliant gameplay! I now love Patchwork and understand why everyone does as well. We find it to be the perfect casual game to whip out for a light chill evening. It is not very competitive as you have your own little game in front of you (to neatly pack every tile you buy) and even better Zeynep doesn't mind losing at all in this. Very fun indeed.

Note: This game has been played several times before I started logging plays.

RATING: 8

If you make it into the midgame in rough equilibrium with your opponent, then the luck element does disappear.  Regardless, it's a fun abstract game which plays fast and has a lot of depth relatively to its low entry barrier.

RATING: 8.5
Uwe Rosenberg should stick to tight, clever 2-player games like this rather than making increasingly languid and sprawling exercises in agricultural worker-placement economy. Patchwork is attractive, intelligent, tactile and very VERY difficult to play well. You'd think we could have our fill of Tetris-like board-fillers, but this one doesn't give any signs that the genre is old.

RATING: 10
[b]Patchwork[/b]

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (10):[/COLOR]

[i]This has been a tough game for me to get get a handle on. While 14 plays may seem like a lot, Patchwork lost some steam as the months rolled on. This game continues to be punishing, especially if you haven't played for a while. I don't mind that though, I always enjoy figuring out how I can actually come out of the game on the + side of the point column. I think it really just comes down to the fact that when I'm picking a quick 2p game I gravitate towards card games. Patchwork is definitely a game I'd recommend and will still continue to get play, just not as much as my family's favorite card games. That said it is still an excellent game and it's actually a punishing Uwe design, which we are seeing less and less of.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (10):[/COLOR]

[i]- Excellent family game that sets up and plays quick, meaning it will hit the table a lot.
- One of the most beautiful games I own, I love the patterns for the quilt pieces.
- Buttons are both your score and income, which really makes this game extremely tense.
- Time track, I love games that use this mechanic, part of your planning has to take into account how many turns in a row you may get or give to the other player.[/i]

心得:
還不錯的小品
一樣一開始可能是要朝衝高收入優先，然後拼圖要想好，免得之後剩太多空格都不能拼
因為版塊一開始隨機排列
遊戲隨機性不錯高
規則:
*起始5鈕扣，隨便一個開始，人token放在2*1的右邊
*動作一 走到對手的前面，過幾格拿多少鈕扣
*動作二，花鈕扣買token前三塊選一，馬上拼，不能疊在一起，拼完在動時間軌，越過鈕扣拿收入，越過1x1補丁就拿走
*先拼出7x7的拿7分獎勵

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Patchwork is a 2-player light filler game in which players are drafting tetris-like patch pieces and trying to fill up their 9x9 grid board. The patch tiles are arranged in a circle around the time track board, along with a pawn that both players use--players can take a tile that’s one to three spaces ahead of the pawn, and then replace the tile they took with the pawn. The tiles have two costs, time and buttons. The time works like Around the World in 80 Days or Thebes; whoever has accumulated the least total time takes the next turn. Buttons introduce a tiny economic element into the game--patch tiles have between zero and three button icons on them, and whenever a player passes a button on the time track, that player receives buttons equal to the number he’s placed on his grid board. There’s a bonus for the first player to fill up a 7x7 area on his grid, but other than that, scoring is just the number of buttons the player has left, minus the spaces on his grid board he didn’t fill. This is a perfectly acceptable filler, but it didn’t really stand out to me.

(1 play)

RATING: 7.5
Easy to play 2p game, really quick and fun, it is great to play with people that don't usually play boardgames.

It is one of Uwe Rosenberg's "test games" that were made while figuring out Feast for Odin, so it has this tetris like style of putting tiles on a board, you have to cover the board with the tiles in order to get points and money is buttons.

I like that it can be pretty unforgiving, since at the end all the squares that are not covered count as -2. In some games the score can be 0 - 4.

It is one of those games you can play multiple times, I like having it on my bag in case I have to wait, I can play with anyone.
