RATING: 7
Who said Uwe doesn't make light games anymore? Huh? No one said that? Okay....

Anyway, after many heavy hitters Uwe returned to make a light game (Bohnanza light) and it is a solid light game. I think it really belongs to a family setting because the game is really light. 

I got to play this game at my local board game meetup and I am glad that I did get to play it at least once to see what the buzz is about.

Player in this game tries to balance time (like Thebes), income (buttons), and geometric patterns (Tetris) in order to win the game with the most buttons.

The decision is light but interesting enough not to disregard it totally. A solid game but not good enough to own as a gamer's game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.75
nice two-player game with a pattern-matching (pseudo-tetris) element. I like that each patch (action) you take costs a different amount of time, which determines how far forward your pawn moves, enabling you to potentially take multiple turns in a row. This adds a little bit more depth of strategy over simply alternating turns as is the case in most games.

I feel that it is a little strategically limited - prioritizing buttons early seems to be a no-brainer, and based on the random order of the patches it may be that one person gets stuck with zero good income-building options. Still, easy to teach and is a unique theme (quilting).

RATING: 7
This is a very cute 2 player game about making a quilt. Players take turn purchasing one of three tetris tiles that are in front of the buying pawn, then move the pawn into the spot that the tile was sitting in, this making different tiles available for the next player. At certain times, the blue button icons pay out buttons, which are one of the currencies used to buy more tiles. When the game ends, players get points for buttons in hand minus heavy penalties for empty spaces. The game buzzes along nicely, and although it's mechanically unremarkable, it's very enjoyable.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:star: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:nostar: Multiple plays stay interesting
:star: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::nostar::nostar: Raw enjoyment
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
My wife works for a quilting magazine, so I was keen to try Patchwork and see if it would be something she might enjoy. My initial impression is positive -- Uwe finally remembered how to design a simple game! It cleverly disguises the bolts of a multi-factor engine-builder under a charming exterior. My concern is that it is too calculable; my hope is that once both players understand those calculations, it will become more interactive. Now I just need to find a copy. Sarah wrote to Mayfair asking for a review copy for her magazine but they haven't responded!

Update after 10 plays: got my own copy, wife loves it, I love it, all fears allayed and all hopes realised!

RATING: N/A
This is a very simple 2p game, and I really like it when Rosenberg does simple. You're managing a few kinds of currency in this one (money/buttons, time, space on your board) and you're sort of creating and solving your own spatial puzzle in the process. And "controlling tempo" is one of my very favorite things to do in gaming, which you get to do here in spades. 

It's a very smooth, quick-playing game. A real delight, and one that feels like it could have been designed at any point in time.

RATING: 6.9
Pros:
* Fun spatial puzzles
* Quick turns that keep both players involved/interested
* There are sufficient opportunities for "spite" moves to allow a healthy level of unpredictability. You can push your luck and set yourself up to need a certain tile, but that just gives your opponent more incentive to keep you from getting it. In some situations this can become a dare of sorts. Set yourself up to need a tile with a highly inconvenient shape and then dare your opponent to take it.
* Simple, consistent and minimal rules.
* Love the Thebes-like time track and how it allows for multiple turns in a row.

Cons:
* Takes up a lot of table space.
* The time board is poorly designed. The circular brown track is better, but it was a mistake to put the patches between spaces; it's too easy to treat that like a separate space. In our last play, on one particular turn we miscounted three times and then frustratingly and very carefully moved one space at a time, dramatically counting out the spaces out loud and on our fingers. It shouldn't be that error prone to move around a board.

Neutral:
* 2 player only (this is a pro for us)
* Victory points are also your currency (I quite like games that do this)


= 2015-07-23 - R:6.8

Played four times so far. Once was a "solo" game against a die that just caused tiles to be removed from the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is not an abstract.

It's a light Euro, economic engine game with a spatial element.

Incredibly attractive components. Very easy on the eyes with its muted colours.

It's a mix of Bunte Runde (object draft), Neuland/Thebes (player turn order), and Universe/Blokus/Kunst Stücke/Domain (playing polyominoes on a board). Actually more like The Princes of Florence as you place polyominoes on your own board, not a shared board.

Very light. Because of the Bunte Runde method of drafting pieces, your choices are typically very limited.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[B]RO:[/B] [I]03/11/2016[/I]

This is a great two-player abstract game. Reminds me strongly of Tetris, but with the theme of making a (very ugly) patchwork quilt. Basically, you are selecting from a wheel of oddly shaped quilt swatches, with only a few being available to you on any turn, you are using these to fill up as much space on your player board as possible. They have two costs, one is time (which will move a marker along a track, when both players are the end the game is over), the other is 'buttons' which acts as the game's currency. At certain points on the time track you will gain buttons for any button symbols on your own quilt pieces, as well as small 1x1 'patches' if you're the first to pass a particular point on the track. You may also acquire buttons by passing and moving the number of spaces required to put your marker in front of your opponent, and collecting that many buttons. If you are behind your opponent on the track it is your turn, in this way you may take multiple turns before your opponent can do anything.

It is very interesting and requires a surprisingly amount of forethought considering the simple mechanics. Further, it is an interesting offering from Uwe Rosenberg whom doesn't usually design this sort of thing (but I do find that while playing it [i]does[/i] feel like one of his designs. Overall, if you're going to be doing a large amount of two-player gaming there is no reason not to pick this one up.

RATING: 8
Very good two player (almost) filler game, with some indirect interaction. It is a spatial puzzle at first glance, but it really has an economic aspect and tradeoff between economy (buttons) and victory points (covered spaces).

Interaction comes with the turn order mechanism, racing for  the bonus patches and which tiles you let be available for your opponent in the next turn; rather subtle, but this is no twoplayer-solitaire.

RATING: 6
Select one of three available pieces to add to your patchwork. Pay a cost in time and 'buttons' (the games money). If you have used more time than your opponent then they now take a turn. It combines a few relatively recent game mechanics (the time track turn ordering) and some popular euro elements (trade offs in future generation of money) into a two player pure abstract. The result is interesting and visually pleasing but I do not think adds any significant depth beyond Knizia's Tutankhamun or Hey That's my Fish! while sacrificing in terms of game length and flexibility on number of players.

RATING: 7
I got this game as a birthday present in December 2015 (the Czech edition, which my wife found cheap - it was sold out for sensible prices here in the UK, luckily the English rules are available online and very straightforward). We played our first game that night, and both enjoyed it (I got thrashed 38-17, which is fairly normal when I play my wife, particularly with a new game). Plenty of non-obvious decisions, while also playing quickly. Neither of us was wowed by it though, I don't really see why this has got so high on the BGG rankings, and neither of us can see this being a game we play all the time. But it's certainly a good game, one that I'm glad I now own, and our opinion may well go up as a result of future plays - which will definitely happen.

Update May 2016: we actually only played our second and third games today, and my opinion basically hasn't changed. A good and interesting game, one I'd usually be happy to play - but nothing special.

RATING: 6
This is a solid little game. The idea of both players making a patchwork quilt with the randomly shaped pieces of cloth that become available is a new mechanic for me. 

It's a pretty simple game to explain and play, but there can be a bit of luck involved in what pieces become available. It's also very important to realise how important buttons are on pieces, especially early. Will also test your Tetris skills a bit!

The game is compact and the pieces are good quality. Though we did go to a craft store and replace all the card buttons (the currency in the game) with actual blue buttons, in 2 sizes. We both feel this really adds to the game.

Overall, a pretty solid game. A bit of a favorite of Layana's. While I don't love it, it's certainly good and quick enough for me to agree to play just about anytime.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.9
solid, solid two player game. some people don't care for the "randomness" in the beginning game layout which could offer one play juicier tiles, but if you've played the game then you know there are ways to delay. in fact, that's the best part of the game: the time track which can allow you to make huge plays, but only if you're willing to give your opponent huge slack to make similar plays or repeat a few smaller plays for tactical advantage. it's a race to accrue the most buttons, but it's also a race to cover the most spaces. you can be efficient with your purchases or efficient with your time, but probably not both. plus, like i said, you have to be aware of what you're allowing your opponent to buy next round. i wouldn't say there's "screwage" or "take-that" so much as there is just some blocking involved. everybody likes tetris. personally, i LOVED the old two-player head-to-head Puzzle Fighter arcade game! well, this is not either of those, but it scratches a similar itch in a bite-sized chunk. quick but not-un-thinky, portable, somewhat windproof, and family themed. this game is a winner.

RATING: 7.5
It's a good abstract 2-player game, and since I dislike 2-player abstracts, that's saying a lot. My wife enjoys it, and we're pretty evenly skilled at it, so that's a big plus. But I don't really understand why it is so popular. The time mechanism similar to Glen More is interesting, but I don't really enjoy how it interacts with racing to claim the one-square leather pieces (we hated the score track bonus tiles in Carc the Castle and played without them). A lot of time can be spent (wasted?) calculating what sequence of moves you should take to guarantee you get the leather and prevent your opponent from getting it. They are basically each worth a 4 point swing, but we may just remove them like we did with Carc.

RATING: 7
Patchwork has already received a lot of play since I received it.  It has to be my favorite 2 player game so far. in Patchwork players try to fill their player boards with all different shapes of quilt pieces to prevent from losing points. The catch is you have to buy these pieces using buttons and spending time to add the piece to your quilt, and buttons are points. 

Pros: unique 2player interaction.simple rules, deep strategic decision making. Fun tile placement aspect. Nice components. 

Cons: not an extremely engrossing theme. Abstract turn order can cause one player to have multiple turns in a row.

RATING: 9
:thumbsup: The polyomino-puzzle is really fun to put together in and of itself. And here it’s combined with resource management: buttons (your points [u]and[/u] the currency with which you buy polyominoes) and time (how often you and your opponent will be able to buy polyominoes).
:thumbsup: The game ‘grows’ with the players. At first you’re just trying to complete your own quilt as efficiently as possible. A few games later, you’ll start eyeing your opponent’s quilt and thinking about how you can further your own efforts while hindering theirs.
:thumbsup: Gorgeous game!
----
:thumbsdown: A shame that it’s only 2-player. It’s a really good 2-player game, but I think it would be a good 3- or 4-player game as well. One could argue that [thing=204027][/thing] or [thing=233678][/thing] are “multiplayer Patchwork”, but that’s really not the case.

RATING: 1.5
At the end of the day it's just another engine builder with matching amount of interaction (gentle queue cutting) and drowned in pedestrian brown pastels. 

[i]Even with a potentially colourful theme, nope, you can't get clean bright colours, we'll drown them in brown so middle aged couples feel comfy around the game and somewhat sedated. Yes, I imagine sewing diagrams for kids and sewing magazines of old and they had white background (!) and clear colours. But somebody had to slap mimetic realism even on (basically) Tetris and this is why we can't have beautiful things. [/i]

Combining engine building with spatial puzzle is kinda original and semi-clever (for time being). But. Even with my SO liking the theme and winning the game and being kinda excited we just ended up trying to find a compromise between cost-efficiency and spatial puzzle and pretty much ignoring the other player. Yes I'm sure if you play the game 90+ times other player will matter (sigh). Almost as much as the random set up... Sooo... it's engine building plus spatial elements minus any sort of narrative progression (like building a church or whathaveyou). Weirdly enough I found soloing Princes of Florence to be more charming (the original version, not the dark brown refry). As for Uwe - Mamma Mia! is our 2 player game of choice. 

[Non-brown version in the Heiko's style, I'd rate a 4.0. Well, it is a bit higher]

RATING: 6.5
Played once. A rather interesting departure from Uwe Rosenberg's repertoire of light card games and heavier resource conversion games, Patchwork has players competing to fill up a personal board with patches of fabric. The options here are limited to choosing one out of three tiles each turn, but there are plenty of elements which have to be considered when making that choice. Players essentially have to juggle between earning buttons, pacing oneself on the time track and attempting to cover the board as much as possible. 

Personally, I felt a little antsy leaving holes on the board when placing pieces, but that's what a childhood spent playing Tetris does to you. The breezy theme and nature of the gameplay is also somewhat marred by the fact that it is very possible to get a negative score – who knew quilting was such a stressful affair? Quibbles aside, Patchwork is a tactical, quick and overall pleasant experience.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Somewhat mathy perfect information abstract. It is easy to calculate the point-value of each piece at any given time, but that is only the first step. Then you have to make sure you don't run of buttons and end up having to waste turns, which means you need to look ahead to know how many buttons you can spare, etc. And you have to calculate the value of every patch, which is not difficult but still takes a bit of time, especially if you aren't good at arithmetic. 

It took me a while to convince Michelle that there is an interesting game in there, but she still isn't particularly fond of it on account of the amount of tedious math involved in every little calculation. Some people treat this as a light, not-too-thinky game, but we won't play it if we aren't prepared to put a lot of thought into it.

RATING: 10
One of my favorite games! The theme seems weird to most people, which I think can be a turn-off. I'll usually describe it as "competitive two-player Tetris" which helps.

Super quick to learn, pretty fast to play, and a LOT of hidden depth. You'll be terrible your first round, but get better really fast. Can't recommend this game enough. It's definitely my favorite two-player game and one I'll always play.

When you're a few turns away from the end, especially if the other player has already finished, I really like calculating what's the overall point differential I can achieve with every possible move.

[2015-05-16]
Uwe bácsi végre elszakadt a zöldségektől és sikerült is nagyot alkotni a Patchworkkel. A kétszemélyes játékban a Firenze hercegeihez hasonlóan a saját 9x9-es táblánkban tetrisezünk különböző ruhadarabokkal. Célunk a teljes tábla minél jobb lefedése. A körünkben a körbe a játék elején véletlenszerűen lerakott ruhadarabok közül mindig az aktuális 3 közül választhatunk, ahol éppen a jelölő jár, utána másik játékos jön. Egy-egy ruhadarab gombba, illetve időbe kerül, amit egy külön táblán jelölünk. Ezen mindig a kevesebb időt felhasználó játékos jön. Ez is ismerős lehet már más játékokból. Tehát igazából sok újdonság nincs, mégis sikerült egy nagyon jó gyurás Uwe mesternek a már meglévő mechanizmusokból. Készített egy szerencsefüggetlen, sokszor újrajátszható játékot két személy részére. Megelőlegezem neki a nagy pontot, ami maximum eggyel csökkenhet, ha a két játék alapján levont erős stratégiám többször bejönne.

[person=10][/person]的兩人抽象遊戲，跟平常種田養牛的農場經營資源轉換工人擺放遊戲完全不同，而且規則簡單卻變化多端超級好玩！俄羅斯方塊的組合堆放概念，加上「花費」和「移動步數」兩個元素，就變成一個需要深思熟慮的兩人遊戲，套上「縫布」的主題還真是滿貼切的！規則簡單時間又短，是兩人遊戲的好選擇！
:star::star::star::star::star:

A two-player abstract game from the worker-placement-resource-conversion-breeding-animals-farming-enthusiastic designer Uwe, which is very easy to learn but provides tons of variability and tough decisions to make in the game. A simple Tetris idea is expanded with two elements, "COST" and "TIME", into a very sophisticated battle. The theme is nicely pasted on and using buttons as the currency is very amusing. Quick, simple, challenging. Highly recommended!

RATING: 8
Patchwork is on the more interesting end of the Kosmos 2p series, along with the travel edition of Ingenious. Granted, it's not actually a Kosmos 2p game, but it might as well be. The box fits. Inside the box there's an engine-building economic game, and a good one--but it's not just a snowball-building exercise. Here the goal is to collect victory points but the primary currency is time, and there's no way to buy more of it. The value of any particular choice is always a bit fuzzy. This is not to say that the game is massively deep; it isn't. But it is way deeper than you would expect for a quick-playing 2p game.

RATING: 8
1 play

This is _very_ good, even though I'm terrible at puzzles! I ended up with a negative score, which is probably how I'll score most often. Still, it's quick and fun!

The rules are very simple: players each start with a 9x9 grid board, and 5 buttons. The time track has spaces for 1-box pieces; place them there. Lay the puzzle pieces in a circle around the board, randomly. Place the token in front of the smallest piece.

The player behind on the time track takes turn(s) until they're in front. On your turn, either:
- take the piece 1-3 spaces ahead of it and put the token in it's place. Pay the price (in buttons) as indicated on the piece, then place it on your board. Advance on the time track by the number of spaces indicated on the piece.
OR
- move your time marker just ahead of the other player, taking 1 button from the bank for each space you advance.

Whenever you advance your time marker past certain spaces on the track, take the size-1 piece and place onto your board.
The first player to completely fill in a 7x7 area of their grid gets the bonus VP. 

The game ends when both players reach the end of the score track. Score 1 point per button, and lose 2 per empty space on your board. Most (positive!) points wins!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
I was really looking forward to this game simply because Uwe Rosenberg is one of, if not my favorite designer.

This is a really simple two-player only game of competitive Tetris.  In this game players will take turns purchasing one of 3 available tiles, all the tiles are laid out at the beginning of the game in a large circle and you can purchase one of the 3 tiles ahead of a pawn placed in this circle.  The tiles all have two costs on them, one in buttons, which is both a form of currency and your victory points at game end, and the other in time.  The tiles are different shapes and sizes and players are trying to fill in as much of their 9x9 grid with these tiles as possible.  Players also progress along a time track and whoever is at the back of the track gets to take a turn, much like in Glen More.  When both players reach the end of the time track the final scores are a player's buttons minus 2x the number of their empty spaces.

There are two ways to get buttons in this game.  One is to forgo purchasing a tile and move your piece to exactly one space ahead of your opponent on the time track getting 1 button for each space moved.  This is incredibly inefficient.  The other way is by passing "income" spaces that give you one button for every button on tiles you've placed.  Some of the tiles have buttons on them.

That's my main gripe with the game, the tiles with buttons on them are so much more  valuable than any of the other tiles.  If you can get a tile with buttons on it, you need to.  This, first of all, needs to be told to new players (it wasn't to me and I lost 40-0) but even then it is the only real strategy.  And sometimes just dumb luck can screw you here.  If none of the next 3 tiles has buttons on it you are stuck either possibly making one available for purchase by your opponent or losing ground by not taking a meaningful turn.  Those tiles just dictate too much of the game.

However, the rest of the game is an enjoyable puzzle and it plays really quickly.  Not bad for an occasional play but still one of my least favorite Rosenberg games.

RATING: 7.75
I adore Patchwork.  A brilliant little Uwe Rosenberg two player game with a theme that's reminiscent of the game Little Big Planet (maybe a little Animal Crossing too?).  But if you aren't into the cutesy sounding theme (because you are an old curmudgeon, I assume?), don't let that turn you off.  There's a lot of strategy in Patchwork as you balance between covering the area of your board in fabric (and patching up any holes), and getting buttons for points.  The Ios for this game is solid too and comes with other thematic options for your patchwork masterpieces.  The only issue I have is that sometimes nearer the end of the game you may feel strapped for options - so thinking about the endgoal you have for your design is a must.

RATING: 7.5
[Mayfair Games 14 edition] {Cloth; tile-laying; 2p} Patchwork is an attractive abstract game.  It has simple rules, good player interaction and high replayability.  It offers short-term decision and long-term planning.

Players are solving puzzling to fill up their board - yet to complete for the necessary patches from the board.  Another challenge is to balance the income and expense.

The only problem of this game is that it needs a big table :)

Some of the patches cannot fit well to each other... Not good.

I like the square score board, but my wife and daughters like the circle one ...
Highly recommended.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
There are two ways to introduce this game in my mind, one very right and one very wrong.

1. Want to play a board game about quilting?
2. Want to play competitive tetris, board game style?

Seriously, the theme, while cute, will not appeal to most male gamers. That SHOULD NOT STOP THEM FROM PLAYING THIS GAME, as it is a marvelous display of game design!  If you can get over a beige castles of burgundy board, you can get over quilting.  

This game is a 2 player only experience.  You take tiles and try to place them on your grid (a la tetris) without leaving any open areas.  The turn and purchasing mechanic are what make this game so appealing.  Buying a piece requires both money and turn priority.  You are constantly balancing in your plans whether you want to give up your cash or allow your opponent more turns to play.  The end result is a fantastic mix of planning ahead, keeping your opponent from buying pieces, and money management.  If you are looking for a 2 player game, this is top dog in my collection.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This is a very easy game to teach someone. It only took me less than 5 minutes to explain all of the components of the game and start playing. Aside from the simplicity, it really takes a bit more planning for someone to win the game. 

To give you an idea on the complexity of the game, you will need to do the following: 
- watch and predict what patch your opponent needs
- plan on the patch you need and what is available
- manage and balance the buttons you have to buy the patch and at the same time to keep as much as you can to win the game
- lastly to fill up your board as much as possible to avoid the penalty at the end of the game

All and all, I truly enjoy this game very much. You can definitely play this game with non-gamer and he/she will still be able to enjoy it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a fun, quick game.  I wouldn't consider it abstract strategy though.  I'd call it a family/strategy game.  It's a light strategy game for two players with great replayability because of the randomness of patch setup.  The randomness also creates quite a luck factor though.  Sometimes the right patches just seem to line up for you and other times they don't.  It seems imperative to get good button income going as early as possible, if you want to do well, but in some games that just isn't possible because of the early layout of buttons available.

One game I will score 30 points and the very next game I will score -5 (negative scores are not uncommon because you lose 2 points for each unoccupied space on your quilt board at the end).  Now between those two games I didn't have a brain aneurism, so what happened?  The patches favored me far more in the first game.  At least that's my excuse. ;)

Still a fun game though with plenty of opportunities to be clever with your moves.  Interaction between the two players doesn't seem apparent at first since you are both working on your own individual quilts, but you soon realize that what your opponent does can affect you greatly and vice versa.  So you are constantly trying to get the upper hand on each other on the time track and the common patch pool.

Overall, a good and enjoyable little strategy game.  Very unique, that's for sure!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Patchwork takes about 5 minutes to setup and about 20 minutes to play. This is a game that you will want to play again and again and one that will stay in your collection permanently if you are anything like me. Uwe Rosenberg has typically designed much heavier more in depth games in the past. To see Mr. Rosenberg design such a lighthearted, quick playing game for 2 players is a refreshing break from some of what he is best known for. I love his heavier designs as well but this is an approachable game that could very well be used as a gateway game for those looking to get into the hobby for the first time, and that is a beautiful thing. This game is about 22 to 25 dollars online and at your friendly local game store and is worth every penny. I rated this game an 8.5 and almost rated it higher than that. The game is that good, and for two players only I’m not sure that there are many out that are better. The reason that this game is so approachable is that it will include a large audience appeal whereas other popular two player titles like Magic The Gathering and Dice Masters will not necessarily appeal to everyone in the family like Patchwork will. This game is one that I would feel comfortable playing with my Grandma and Grandpa. It might be a bit tougher to get some of my family excited about piloting a Goblin Aggro deck from Magic The Gathering to victory. There is beauty in the simplicity of this game but there is also such strategic depth that it will draw in new gamers and seasoned tabletop players alike.

RATING: 8
A new 2-player favorite.

Major props to the publishers for going with a theme that was fairly risky. Yes, Quilt Show broke that ground and showed that a game with a quilting theme could be well received, but still. You've got to think there were many others that were safer.

The mechanic for acquiring the patches is innovative and keeps the tactical decisions simple by limiting what you can buy now, but does allow for strategic planning by showing you everything available in the near AND long term. It makes for a nice blend of planning and makes for a perfect information game that does not promote AP. This is the genius of the game.

I think it also uses the turn order mechanic from Neuland and Glen More to good effect. It allows for more control and gives opportunities for clever play. Most importantly, without it, the patch buying thing doesn't work. The calculation would be so dry and predictable that the game would both take longer and be much less interesting.

This is the first time I've ever said this about a Mayfair game, but they got everything right.




Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 3
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 2
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 1
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 2

RATING: 7
Great little 2 player game, with a lot of replayability. The set up means that every game is different, and strategies do start to emerge the more you play. Beginners will focus on their own boards, making the game a bit of a solitaire initially, but soon enough, you'll be watching that other board and considering not just the shapes but also the scoring value of your pieces. If you have an opponent that you can play over and over with, you scores will slowly get closer and closer until every game becomes a fairly tight strategic affair.

Great for introducing casual players to more advanced game play concepts.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Patchwork is a two player game where you are trying to fill your board (a 9 x 9 grid) with "fabric" pieces as completely as possible. At the end of the game empty spots count against your score 2 pts each. Pieces come in a variety of shapes, each with a cost in buttons and time.

On your turn you buy one of the three pieces at the front of the line. You pay the buttons and advance on the time track as many spaces as it cost in time. The piece designating the beginning of the line moves to the space where the piece you took was (so if you skip some pieces, they move to the end of the line).

If you choose not to buy a piece, or can't due to lack of money or space restrictions, then you advance on the time track to a spot one space ahead of your opponent. You collect a button for every space you advanced. Whoever is further back on the time track takes the next turn. If you ever move onto your opponent's piece, you are considered "further back" on the time track.

Additionally, if you ever cross a button icon on the time track, then all the buttons on pieces you've put onto your board pays you a button. There's also some "patches", single square pieces, that are awarded to the first player to pass them.

When you reach the end of the time track, you're done. You wait for your opponent to be done and then you score. Every empty space on your board docks you two points, every button you own gives you a point (the last spot on the board triggers a last button income). There's also a 7 point bonus for the first person to complete a fully filled in 7 x 7 section.

I didn't really know what to expect from this game. It's a clever game where timing is very important. Knowing when to spend a lot of time is crucial. You want your opponent to spend a lot of time, so that you can buy a lot of pieces while he gets no turns. But some pieces give you a lot of button income, or fill a lot of space, or fit the weirdly shaped gap you've left yourself, and so you may be willing to spend extra time to snag them. And of course, you want to time things so that you can pick up the special single-space patches.

Although I've only played it against the AI, I've enjoyed the game a fair bit. It's more fun than many other abstracts. The quilt theme goes a long way towards making the game feel less abstract. I don't know if this is a game I'd enjoy as much over the board, but it makes for a great time-waster app.

RATING: 8
About [thing=163412][/thing]:

[b]1) What is it?[/b]
[thing=163412][/thing] is a two players game in which the goal is to make the best quilt. Sure, it doesn't sound all that exciting, but sometimes you just need a relaxing time with a partner, right? Some soothing moments, taking some tiles and arranging them, tetris-style, in a personal board with a 9x9 grid.

[thing=163412][/thing] demands little and give a lot. The rules are very easy to teach and the gameplay as smooth as it can be. Most of the time you will be taking tiles and putting them on your board, in a way that few open spaces remain - there is no point to a quilt with holes all over it.

The interaction is mostly indirect - taking something the other might want -, with some dispute over the leather tiles. Hurt feelings won't happen all that often. I guess is possible to play more aggressively, wanting to push the other to unplaceable tiles, however this seems to me like a proper way to put yourself in a dead end.

[thing=163412][/thing] is a quick game, very well knitted together, with important decisions to be made throughout.

[b]2) How do you play?[/b]
Each player starts with 5 buttons. Every turn the player must do one of two actions:
a) Take a tile, pay the number of buttons required and advance, on the time track, the number of indicated spaces;
b) Advance on the time track until your token is one space in front of the other player - gain 1 button per space advanced.

When you take a tile you must immediately put it on your board, and the tile can't be moved once is put there.

Some tiles have buttons on them. When you reach certain spots on the time track, you will get an income of buttons equal to the number of buttons your tiles have. Also, some places on the track have tiles of special patch - 1x1 in size. The first person to reach these spaces get the tile and put them on her board - this is very good to fill some holes on the quilt.

The time track serves not only to mark income and to take leather squares. It also serves to mark whose turn it is. The person behind on the time track is the person in turn. And this person plays until she passes the other player, which can mean multiple plays in a row.

Finally, once both players reach the end of the time track, the game ends. Buttons are worth 1 point each. For every space not covered, the player loses 2 points. There is also a goal token - the first player (if any) to fill a 7x7 grid, gains the goal token, which is worth 7 points at the end of the game. The person with the most points, after deducting for the uncovered spaces, will be the winner!

[b]3) Which are the decisions made during play?[/b]
Mostly will be what tile to buy. This is a three fold decision:
a) The cost of it, the time it will advance you and if it has or not buttons for income - this affects, of course, the amount of money you will have for your next purchase and the position on the time track, which may allow for another go for yourself, to trigger income, or give you one of the coveated special patch tiles;
b) The shape of it - not only to fit in your board, but also how big it is, as you also need to cover as much space as possible;
c) Which position the marker will end, as tiles restricts the next buying phase - for you, if you are going to play again (still behind in time) or, more likely, to your opponent.

Even though it has ramifications, the decision isn't hard, specially because you will only have three options of tiles to take, and one or two you might not even be able to fit or to pay for.

The other decision is when to "jump" in time, in order to gain buttons to pay for things. This is a thing to avoid - jumping is objectively a bad move most of the time, as you lose precious time not filling your board, and since for every square open you will lose 2 points, and a button is worth 1 point, is almost like you lose 1 point for every space jumped. Still, this will be need, but usually won't be a decision on itself - you will simply do it because you can't pay for any of the next three tiles.

[b]4) What are the good things in the game?[/b]
- It is beautiful, with a good graphic design and comes in a small box, very good to store and to take around;
- Language independant;
- Easy to teach and to play;
- Short playing time;
- The random order of the tiles makes for a simple way to increase replay value;
- Some interaction, but not enough to leave people mad (usually very important in a 2 player game), in a low pressure environment;
- It is super nice to fill the board with the tiles.

[b]5) Which are the bad news?[/b]
- Only for 2 players;
- No solo rules;
- Too friendly for those looking for high confrontational and bloody 2 player game.

[b]6) How do you feel while playing?[/b]
There is something very satisfying in seeing that blank board slowly filling up with shapes and colors, with some cute blue buttons showing. It reminds me of the the hint of life and colors just around the corner in that winter days, and the promise of heat and peace, in a warm room with a good book. It offers a sense of advancement, like an unfolding story, in a comfy and inviting enviroment.

I don't usually like 2 players game - not that I don't enjoy confrontation, but I get tense and stressed when is a head-to-head thing, as it feels that, even when 2 players are battling, but there are more people involved, some steam is let loose or redirected. Therefore, I usually lean towards friendlier 2 players game, either cooperative ones, like [thing=71836][/thing], or with most indirect interaction, like [thing=28143][/thing] or [thing=50][/thing], with just some highly thematic games passing this bar, such as [thing=36932][/thing], [thing=45986][/thing] and [thing=115746][/thing], or extra quick, like [thing=147020][/thing]. [thing=163412][/thing] is more in line with [thing=50][/thing] than with [thing=147020][/thing], with the kicker of building your own board, which is something I adore doing in games.

[thing=163412][/thing] is always pushing its way to the end - every turn it gets closer and closer, never stopping, but there is truly no stress in here: you have your time to pick, and there is only truly 4 possibilities each turn - either to take one of the three tiles after the marker, or jump on the track to gain some buttons.

In the end, [thing=163412][/thing] hits several buttons (he) without dropping the stitch a single time. It is quick, efficient and ever going forward, without adding too much pressure. Very recommended.

RATING: 6
I don't get this one.  I love Uve Rosenberg, I play 2-player games primarily, I'm not turned off by the theme, and everyone else except my wife and I seem to enjoy this game.

This is not to say it's a terrible game, but it's really quite basic and while the calculations involved in using space vs. collecting buttons is somewhat interesting, I think I expected more out of the Tetris-like puzzle.  

You do have to solve it like a Tetris puzzle if you are planning to be the first to collect the 7x7 bonus tile points, but if you are going another strategy, or after that tile has been acquired, any Tetris puzzle really goes out the window.  So many games come down to only being able to purchase one of 3 tiles, of which only one will fit in my puzzle.  And this is not because I'm not doing a good job filling up the board... it's mostly full. It's just a little lackluster and you really can't count on a certain shape coming around when you need it toward the end of the game.

Still a short game that provides something new/unique and can be enjoyable -- I'm just really unimpressed and a little frustrated with the endgame.

RATING: 6.5
Pros: unique tile placement and/or puzzle mechanic, easy to learn, quick playtime

Cons: limited strategic & tactical options, no player interaction, can be swingy, low level of replayability

Easy to learn with intuitive rules and elegant flow, this is a good two-player filler game that fits right into an enjoyable, relaxing evening with the wife. For what it sets out to do, it is great, but I prefer games with more player interaction. It can also feel a little repetitive--I have never desired to play it back-to-back. My other complaint is that sometimes there's some significant point swings, depending on opportunities to get higher-valued tiles and the 7x7 special tile, which can be susceptible to a lot of luck.

RATING: 5
good little 2p game with 2 kinds of "time track" mechanic I like

[+] the whole track of tile offers some very interesting choices (how much am I willing to pay, what am I giving up on the way, what possibilities am I opening for my oponent), the milestones (scoring, bonus) on the time track offer a second level of objectives, I like the spatial puzzle element of racing to fill a 7x7 area
[-] maybe I need to play more but it feels that some tiles are way better than other (mainly those that cost very little time) because the cost of not filling up your board is so high that you have to get has many tiles as possible, and the only way to do that is to get a bunch of cheap -in terms of time- ones

RATING: 7.5
So my wife would often joke about acquiring Patchwork, and I would vociferously protest in response. "A quilting game?? Ha ha...no." But then, after reading so many glowing reviews, I finally decided to capitulate. The game definitely has a certain level of appeal to me--it is Tetris-like, so it is rather satisfying when all but a few of the squares on my board are filled in at game's end. On the other hand, when I end the game with -10 points, I feel like the true quilting novice that I am. I wouldn't hesitate to play this game occasionally, but it's not one that I would include among my top choices for lighter games.

RATING: 8
Patchwork is a cross between spatial puzzle and economic snowball, but despite those two completely self-absorbed elements the game achieves a pleasant level of interaction due to the time-based turn order mechanism previously seen in Thebes and Neuland. I'm impressed- the game squeezes a lot of depth out of very few moving parts. I suspect Patchwork will actually get better with repeated plays as players become more comfortable with the spatial puzzle and can increasingly turn their focus to the tactical battle over tile selection. I'd like to own this game.

RATING: 7.5
Do you like tetris? Then you should get this game! A lot of strategy in a small box based on the logic of tetris. Which piece should I get? The one that is expensive in buttons or the one that will cost me more time? Or should I just surpass my opponent to obtain more buttons and that single tile? I love the interaction and the thinking that you have to do in order to plan your next moves (if the opponent acts the way he is supposed to) as well as the goal of creating a 7X7 square to get the 7 points which is a huge advantage in the end. I think that it could have been designed for more players (at least 2 more). For its price, it's a bargain!

RATING: 6.8
I bought this game to play with my wife with the objective to get her introduced into boardgames. Since the theme is patchwork and not fantastic worlds I thought that she would more interested, and it worked! My wife enjoyed it a lot :)

The game is clever, and original, basically you have to build a puzzle (fill a 9x9 table) with pieces that you buy each time. A feature of the game I like is that you don´t play one move each turn, instead, the player that is last on the path always plays, so it makes you choose carefully what piece you buy. 

The pieces of the puzzle have several characteristics which make them more or less interesting  1) the shape of the piece 2) number of bottoms on the piece (more bottoms will generate more income during the game), number of spaces you will be forced to advance on the board (the smaller the better), 3) cost of the piece.

It is a very easy game to play but still interesting one.

RATING: 8
R
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I certainly didn't see this one coming. An Uwe Rosenberg game about quilt making. It has none of the usual modern Uwe trappings either. No worker placement, no resource swapping or anything else we've gotten used to in the last few years. The main mechanic is basically a tile drafting tetris game, set up like a big rondel made up of all the pieces. On your turn, you can buy one of the next three pieces in front of the pawn to add to your quilt. If you can't, then you pass and collect some money. That's really all there is to it.

It is super fast and quite addicting. A perfect nightcap or lunch break game, for sure.

RATING: 9.5
Played a borrowed copy of this with everyone in the family. A beautifully designed and balanced game, where you buy fabric swatches of different shapes to fill out your "quilt". It's like Tetris, except the shapes are much more varied, and other decisions come into play. The mechanics of turns, purchasing, gaining income, and scoring are incredibly well thought-out, and make for an easy to learn, and easy to play game. My family doesn't like games that are too "thinky", and they all loved this one. We gave it back to our neighbors who loaned it to us, and we immediately missed it.

RATING: 7.3
A bit of an oddball for me. I like the concept and generally enjoy playing, but if my opponent is taking it seriously the turns can drag and it kills it for me.

Look at it like this, in my head I view the game almost like actual Tetris. Because of this I make my piece choice as best I can while trying to keep it as fast as possible, so I could end up with some sub optimal choices/placements (which is fine), and I find the thrill of it quite fun. But when matched with an opponent who takes 3+ minutes per turn to carefully decide on which piece they're going to take I shutdown and it starts to become hair pullingly long.

So I think it's a good game overall, and I feel that either approach is perfectly fine. You can really make this game to be whatever you want, but just be sure that you'll be playing with someone who's approaching it the same as you.

RATING: 7.8
A wonderful, fast two player game that I believe belongs in everyone's collection because of its simple, elegant design that offers a rich, deep gameplay experience in a such a short time.  This is truly one of Uwe's best games.  The Tetris style pieces remind me of building in Amerigo.  This game has interesting choices to make.  The resources in my opinion are buttons (which are points and currency), time, and space on your board.  Every empty space at the end of the game is -2 points so sometimes you take tiles that are larger but don't give you a good payout on buttons or time during the game so that you can do a better job at filling your board spaces.  Buying tiles that cost a lot of time uses your time resource but allows you to get the 1 x 1 tiles before your opponent does.  Buying tiles with lots of button symbols can help you a lot during the early game because those symbols pay out every time you cross a blue button throughout the game but aren't as critical towards the end of the game when you're hoping to just fill up your board.  I love this game because you can also plan your moves ahead and hope that your opponent doesn't take that crucial tile you need.  Maybe the best bang for your buck game out there!  This game also has the added plus that it will more than likely appeal to your wife!  My wife really likes it!

Note: Includes real blue wooden buttons for currency.

RATING: 6
This game is cute and charming. I want to share it with as many people as possible. It has a really fun theme that works for the mechanics. The gameplay is nice and comfy. Placing pieces feels like a puzzle, getting buttons feels like engine-building, drafting pieces takes strategy.
The main problem I see with this game is replayability as it really doesn't vary much each playthrough (starting tile configurations change nothing). After the one game I played of it i have no real desire to play again even though I had a lot of fun. I am not sure it is collection worthy, unless your looking for some comfy padding.
